## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator by including nonlinear restoring forces (functions of x), nonlinear damping (functions of v), and possibly explicit time-dependent driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced cubic oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (parametric excitation)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity / asymmetric potential)
- Damped Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v
- General polynomial restoring + damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v
- Nonlinear damping with quadratic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * x**3
- Driven oscillator with nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * (1 + c3 * x**2) + c4 * sin(c5 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) indicate symmetric potential wells (Duffing-type), while even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials (Helmholtz-type)
- Velocity-position coupling terms like v*x² are signatures of amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type nonlinear dissipation)
- Explicit sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Product terms x*cos(c*t) indicate parametric excitation where a system parameter oscillates in time
- Sign of the cubic coefficient relative to the linear term distinguishes hardening (same sign restoring) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence in the acceleration formula indicates an autonomous system where energy considerations (conservative + dissipative) fully determine dynamics
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v³) represent dissipative forces, while even powers of velocity (v²) can represent direction-dependent drag
- When damping coefficient depends on x² (e.g., c*(x²-1)*v), this creates limit cycle behavior with self-sustained oscillations
